  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a6d43ba5-d56c-447a-926b-9f1df03f125d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText6716159351737442887" style="display:none"><b>Following the shocking revelations of DARK DAYS, get ready for the fifth instalment of the bestselling Skulduggery Pleasant series -- guaranteed to contain at least 40% humour, 50% action, and 100% thrills!</b><br /><br /><i>The blonde girl with the black lips turned to Valkyrie. 'We know,' she said. 'We've seen the future. We know you're going to kill the world!'</i> <br /><br />Skulduggery Pleasant and Valkyrie Cain are back -- just in time to see their whole world get turned upside down! While they struggle to protect a known killer from an unstoppable assassin, Valkyrie is on a secret mission of her own. This quest, to prevent her dark and murderous destiny, threatens to take her to the brink of death and beyond. And then the body-snatching Remnants get loose, thousands of twisted souls who possess the living like puppets, and they begin their search for a being powerful enough to lead them. Facing such insurmountable odds, Skulduggery, Valkyrie, Ghastly and Tanith can trust no one. Not even each other!</span>

<div id="review_1187814336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1187814336" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1187814336?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1187814336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6943166581107223320"><b>BASICALLY I HATE THIS BOOK AND BY "HATE" I MEAN I LOVE IT SO SO MUCH.</b> It was completely dark and scary and sad and, wow. Goodbye happy days where the book ended with Val getting some family time, sleep, and possibly a better meal than cold cereal. (Although I question the lack of meals in these series, but HEY. It's magic.) <i>So much happened...</i> Gah. Where do I even begin??<br/><br/>Pfft. I'll begin with: <b>I LOVE THIS SERIES SO MUCH.</b> I recommend it 2 thousand percent. Literally the only thing I have issues w</span>
  <span id="freeText6943166581107223320" style="display:none"><b>BASICALLY I HATE THIS BOOK AND BY "HATE" I MEAN I LOVE IT SO SO MUCH.</b> It was completely dark and scary and sad and, wow. Goodbye happy days where the book ended with Val getting some family time, sleep, and possibly a better meal than cold cereal. (Although I question the lack of meals in these series, but HEY. It's magic.) <i>So much happened...</i> Gah. Where do I even begin??<br /><br />Pfft. I'll begin with: <b>I LOVE THIS SERIES SO MUCH.</b> I recommend it 2 thousand percent. Literally the only thing I have issues with is the amount of characters and the fact that I, with my awful memory, forget them so so often. I mixed up Wreath and Ghastly Bespoke, can you believe. *facepalm* I wish to fire my own brain sometimes, but, eh, you know. That would be awkward. <br /><br /><b>ALSO SO MUCH PAAAAAAIN.</b> Did I mention how much PAIN?!! DEATH! And <i>worse</i> than death. I need a moment for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kenspeckle who I loved a huge amount and is now DEAD and HOW COULD THEY LET THIS HAPPEN?!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I also need a moment just to swallow and gently reassure myself that I can borrow book 6 ASAP from the library. CLIFFHANGER. Although, I admit, not as bad as book 4's cliffhanger. *ahem*<br /><br /><b>So now we know Val is Darquesse....but worse, there are Rements everywhere.</b> Basically evil ghosts. They cause havoc. And let's just say this isn't an author who spares his characters. He absolutely TORTURES them. And there is a horrible, gross, freaky scene where Val nearly dies. But, it's kind of like the TV show Supernatural, where all the good characters die a few times. *shrugs* It gets to be normal. After all, Skulduggery is kinda dead 24/7, bless him. <br /><br /><b>The humour is SO GOOD.</b> There are action scenes (which I complained about in the first books because they were long and unengaging, but they're now <i>perfectly</i> written) and then there is hilarious humour and then there are TEARS AND PAIN. I love the balance. And, yes the book is like 500+ pages, and I do think it could've been a little smaller...but I really enjoyed it 100% of the time. There was always something going down. There are no fluffy chapters. Although Fletcher and Val do go to a dance, but pffft, as if that ends well. HA AH. No. Unfortunately there was less time with the Edgley family which makes me sad because I LOVE Val's parents. (And yes I say "Val" instead of "Valkyrie" because I have to look up every time I type her full name and I am lazy and also not a good speller apparently.)<br /><br />Oh, but there was one line that's stolen out of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21787.The_Princess_Bride_" title="The Princess Bride  by William Goldman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Bride</a> and I'm not REALLY sure how that is legal/possible?? It was funny, but it did concern me a little. <br /><br /><blockquote>"You seem to have me beaten," he said at last.<br />"So it seems. But if this is true, then why are you smiling?"<br />"Because," Dalrymple answered, "I know something you don't know."<br />"And what is that?" asked Skulduggery. <br />"I'm not right-handed," Dalrymple replied.</blockquote><br /><br />Tell me that's not STRAIGHT from The Princess Bride?! BECAUSE IT IS. Hmph. <br /><br /><b>Also there's a bit less of Skulduggery.</b> I think Val is strong on her own now, and doesn't always need him to scrape her off the ground. For instance: she can actually get out of her own predicaments, which I LOVE AND ADORE. I love girls who don't need anyone to rescue them. But I did miss having Skulduggery around. And also it hints that Val and Skulduggery's relationship is a bit unbalanced right now. Like Val is a little scared of him....I'm curious to see if this develops more.<br /><br />Basically: <b>I WANT TO KNOW ALL THE THINGS AND I WANT TO KNOW THEM NOW.</b> But I have to mentally prepare myself for the next book. *sobs* I can't believe <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Tannith has a remnent attached to her. NOOOOO. Although I do question why everyone is like "there is no hope for Tannith" when everyone else had remnents in them and they're okay now?! Did I miss something??? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Definitely love this series. It is so underrated. All the humans of the universe need to read these. SO FUNNY AND SAD.<br /><br />****<br /><br /><b>NOTABLE QUOTES OF HILARITY:</b><br /><br /><blockquote>"When this is over," he [Ghastly] continued, "I'm going to make you dinner. You don't have to like it, and you don't have to eat it, and I suppose you don't even have to be there, but...But that's what I'm going to do."<br />Tannith frowned. "Are you asking me on a date?"<br />"I think so, yes. Will you have dinner with me?"</blockquote><br /><br />*whispers* I ship it. <br /><br /><blockquote>Valkyrie smiled patiently. "I like how you do your make-up. Do you use a brush, or just dip your head in the bucket?"</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Fletcher, Stephanie tells us you're in college. How's tha going?"<br />"Really well," Fletcher said, trying to smile. "I'm doing economics. That's teh study of the economy. I love it."<br />"Which college?"<br />"Hmm?"<br />"Which college do you go to?"<br />Fletcher nodded. "Yes."<br />"I'm sorry."<br />"Oh," Fletcher said, and laughed.<br />"He's not good with first impressions," Valkyrie said sadly. "He doesn't know what he's saying. We should go before he starts to dribble." </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Wow," she said. "It's like you're teaching me something and being all wise."<br />"You are not easy to get along with," Skulduggery said.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Seriously?"<br />"Yes."<br />"So he has no head?"<br />"That's usually what headless means."<br />"No head at all?"<br />"You're really getting hung up on this headless thing aren't you?"<br />"It's just kind of silly, even for us."<br />"Yet you spend your days with a living skeleton."<br />"But at least Skulduggery has a head."<br />"True."<br />"He even has a spare."<br />"Are we going to get past this now?"<br />"Yes. Sorry. Carry on."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"It's going to be a bunch of people talking about what we're going to do about setting up a new Sanctuary. What do I have to contribute to <i>that</i>?"<br />"I don't know. A general air of grumpiness?"</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"We saw Darquesse, <i>me</i>, as a figure in the distance, fighting and killing and murdering, and then we saw me, my <i>future</i> self, close up, feeling pretty bad about it all, which is nice of her, but she's undoubtedly a little fruitloops."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6943166581107223320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I can honestly not recommended this series enough!</span>

<div id="review_137240099" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137240099" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2097698-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241012301p2/2097698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137240099?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/2097698-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137240099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3326428106031433492">This was by far the thickest, and like, one of the most incredible books ever! Hands down the best in the series. Everything is witty and dry as usual, and Derek Landy even succeeded in making me tear up at one point. I also went "Oh shit," among other things a couple of times. You know it's a good book when you can laugh, cry, and swear while reading it. In fact, I loved this so much, I won't even bother trying to spoil anything, because the momentum would keep me going until I'd written the wh</span>
  <span id="freeText3326428106031433492" style="display:none">This was by far the thickest, and like, one of the most incredible books ever! Hands down the best in the series. Everything is witty and dry as usual, and Derek Landy even succeeded in making me tear up at one point. I also went "Oh shit," among other things a couple of times. You know it's a good book when you can laugh, cry, and swear while reading it. In fact, I loved this so much, I won't even bother trying to spoil anything, because the momentum would keep me going until I'd written the whole book down right here, and I'm pretty sure that's probably illegal.<br /><br />Only... know this, Derek Landy, I'm on to you. I know that you've read the Princess Bride, I know you've read Twilight (I love your new and improved, plus more realistic, reaction to people who come on like that), and I know you watched Monty Python ("Ex-rabbit." Hah!) , and that you watch Doctor Who. With the exception of Dr Who, which I found out you watch from reading your blog, I know all this because you made your own clever little parodies and twists on some of the lines and/or situations. And being able to appreciate these mini-references, we'd probably be total best buds if we met! ... huh... how did I get here? Anyway, keep writing Derek, and pour on the awesomeness! Unless for some unknown reason, your style or plots begins to take a turn for the worse, I will never tire of reading the adventures of Valkyrie and Skulduggery! Face it. The way you write it, Skulduggery spends a good deal of his time unconscious while Valkyrie is the one going all butt-whooping mode. Please try and do something with the Skul-man other than giving him your best witty remarks and nick-o'-time appearances.<br /><br />Also, I always <i>knew</i> you had something against Tanith Low, you heartless <i>bastard</i>. But Kenspeckle? <i>Really?</i> Who the hell is going to fix 'em now? <i>Nye?</i> ~scoffs~</span>
  <a data-text-id="3326428106031433492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11428142749009403988"><blockquote> <b>"Plans are an invitation to disappointment." </b> </blockquote><br/>I'm disappointed, too.   <span id="freeText11428142749009403988" style="display:none"><blockquote> <b>"Plans are an invitation to disappointment." </b> </blockquote><br />I'm disappointed, too. Disappointed that it took me three days to finish this book when it clearly could have been done faster because it was so fricking good. But my body decided it needed more sleep than usual. Damn it. Where was I? Ah, Skulduggery. I loved this series from book 1 and I can't help loving it more with each book and even the reread won't get boring because there are so many little things you tend to forget and the bickering between the charackters (who I all adore in their own way) just make it a really fun read. This book had so much important stuff happening (and I don't mean me getting more and more into wondering if there's a ship name for Valkyrie and Skulduggery? I mean, in these books she's still a little young so I'm fine with the current relationship status but...) and there are so many characters coming out to play, there's a little foreshadowing of what's to come and it's gonna be huge! <br />Anyway, I feel like I'm rambling. I love this book. Go and read this series if you like sarcastic characters and magic.</span>

<div id="review_119159222" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119159222" />
    <a title="Darren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3530438-darren"><img alt="Darren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326022184p2/3530438.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119159222?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darren" href="/user/show/3530438-darren">Darren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3530438-darren?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119159222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10495200180818019018">In preparation for writing this review I have just looked back at what I wrote about Dark Days, the previous book in this hugely entertaining series. At the time I really struggled to write a detailed review that did not contain any spoilers, and I'm now having that Groundhog Day feeling. Please do not feel let down if this review is not as detailed as some of my others but given the recent backlash on blogs and Twitter about certain nasty reviewers peppering their <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7260188.Mockingjay__Hunger_Games___3_' title='Mockingjay (Hunger Games, #3) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mockingjay</a> reviews with spoile</span>
  <span id="freeText10495200180818019018" style="display:none">In preparation for writing this review I have just looked back at what I wrote about Dark Days, the previous book in this hugely entertaining series. At the time I really struggled to write a detailed review that did not contain any spoilers, and I'm now having that Groundhog Day feeling. Please do not feel let down if this review is not as detailed as some of my others but given the recent backlash on blogs and Twitter about certain nasty reviewers peppering their <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7260188.Mockingjay__Hunger_Games___3_" title="Mockingjay (Hunger Games, #3) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">Mockingjay</a> reviews with spoilers I want to be extra careful with this.<br /><br />This is the thickest Skulduggery Pleasant book so far, weighing in at a hefty 572 pages; Derek Landy has obviously been on something of a writing roll given that Dark Days was released a mere five months ago. I enjoyed Dark Days but I had some reservations about how certain villains could have been developed more and a couple of the scenes seemed slightly superfluous. You will be glad to hear that I have no such criticisms about this book at all - I loved it and I think it has possibly become one of my favourite of the series so far.<br /><br />Dark Days ended with less of a cliffhanger than its predecessor The Faceless Ones, although the final revelation about Darquesse was more than enough to get Skulduggery fans speculating wildly on fan forums and Facebook. Mortal Coil will not answer all of the questions that have been asked over the last five months, but the plot does have a number of deeply pleasing revelations. However, at the same time it also creates even more questions regarding Valkyrie, Darquesse et al so expect those forums to be buzzing noisily over the next few months as well.<br /><br />The plot of Dark Days relied partly on the villains' use of a Remnant - a body-snatching wraith-like entity that can take over and use a human body without others realising. In Mortal Coil the Remnants play much more than a cameo role - the plot very much focuses on these creatures as they are released from their prison in the Midnight Hotel with devastating consequences for our team of heroes and the local 'normal' population. Yes.... people die in this book (and not just nameless mortals either), and sometimes pretty nastily, although Derek Landy rarely resorts to giving us graphic descriptions of this as he much prefers his readers to use their imaginations to fill in all the gory details. However, there is one wonderful scene where Valkyrie takes herself off to be 'treated' (any other word would give too much away) and the description of her experience is certainly not for the faint hearted!<br /><br />Much of this book focuses on how Valkyrie is coming to terms with the revelations at the end of Dark Days, especially with regards to issues of trust. In her mind, despite being very close to Skulduggery, Tanith, Fletcher and the others, she is really not sure she trusts any of them enough to help her in this case. This leads to her putting her life in mortal peril, without any of them aware, and then, just as she feels she is able to confide a little more in her friends along come the Remnants and suddenly no-one knows who can they trust. Once the Remnants appear en masse the reader is kept guessing for the rest of the book as to just who has, or hasn't, been taken over and Derek Landy treats us to more nail biting scene after nail biting scene, some of which had me completely stumped as to how our heroes would escape death, or something worse, and as for the final climactic scene....... you will just have to read it for yourself, but I have a very strong feeling it will shock you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10495200180818019018" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16969674799651171789">I'm pretty sure the power is going to go out any minute now, so I have to make this quick lmao<br/><br/>- Enjoyed this one as much as the others. I honestly don't know if it's nostalgia or whether I'm just genuinely really enjoying these books and these characters, but either way: I'm having a great time!<br/>- I remember reading these books as they were coming out when I was a kid and then teenager, so it must not have bothered me at the time, but some of the scenes in this book are preeeetty damn gory and da</span>
  <span id="freeText16969674799651171789" style="display:none">I'm pretty sure the power is going to go out any minute now, so I have to make this quick lmao<br /><br />- Enjoyed this one as much as the others. I honestly don't know if it's nostalgia or whether I'm just genuinely really enjoying these books and these characters, but either way: I'm having a great time!<br />- I remember reading these books as they were coming out when I was a kid and then teenager, so it must not have bothered me at the time, but some of the scenes in this book are preeeetty damn gory and dark. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There's a scene where a vivisection of sorts is performed on Valkyrie, something she watches happen, and her heart is removed for Plot Reasons. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It wasn't too bad, really, but I remember being like "Bit full on for a kid's book!" while I was reading. Am I just getting old? Who knows.<br />- <i>REALLY</i> not a fan of the budding love triangle, it was definitely my least favourite aspect of the novel. Luckily it's mostly in the background of the story, so it's not enough for me to remove a star, but... If it ends up being a bigger part of the plot... That's gonna be a problem for my love-triangle-hating ass.<br />- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I completely forgot about some of the character deaths in this novel, as well as the permanent remnant possession of Tanith, so!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I'm a sad mess right now! What a fun time!<br />- I love China Sorrows a <i>lot</i>. Best girl. We love a queen.<br /><br />Onto book six! It's the last book in the series I remember reading as a teenager, so after that everything's going to be all new and surprising. Can't wait!</span>

<div id="review_179493763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179493763" />
    <a title="Crazyjamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3025308-crazyjamie"><img alt="Crazyjamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321964208p2/3025308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179493763?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crazyjamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crazyjamie" href="/user/show/3025308-crazyjamie">Crazyjamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007326013" href="/book/show/9767135-mortal-coil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179493763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5836398620292052182">Mortal Coil is the fifth book in Derek Landy's entertaining fantasy series, and sees a continuation of the overarching storyline that emerged in the fourth book. Valkyrie Cain continues to enjoy her life as the side kick of Skulduggery Pleasant, along with her other supernatural friends and her new boyfriend Fletcher Renn. However, her apparent future as Darquesse continues to hang over her, driving her to take drastic steps to change her fate. Elsewhere, the Necromancers decide to possess Finba</span>
  <span id="freeText5836398620292052182" style="display:none">Mortal Coil is the fifth book in Derek Landy's entertaining fantasy series, and sees a continuation of the overarching storyline that emerged in the fourth book. Valkyrie Cain continues to enjoy her life as the side kick of Skulduggery Pleasant, along with her other supernatural friends and her new boyfriend Fletcher Renn. However, her apparent future as Darquesse continues to hang over her, driving her to take drastic steps to change her fate. Elsewhere, the Necromancers decide to possess Finbar Wong using their entrapped Remnant to determine whether or not Valkyrie is to become the Deathbringer. But plans take a turn for the worse when the Remnant escapes, with the single minded aim to release the thousands of other Remnants trapped within Anton Shudder's hotel. <br /><br />In my review of the fourth book I made the point that it changed the feel of the series so far by concentrating on an overarching storyline as well as an individual plotline. That change continues with this book to the point where it could be said that the overarching plotline now takes precedent over the individual one. To that end this book does start slowly, with the first couple of hundred pages exploring the attempts of the Irish Sanctuary to rebuild after the events of the last book. As ever some new characters are introduced, with the Russian assassin Tesseract being a highlight, but the main plotline after those initial couple of hundred pages centres around the outbreak of Remnants. <br /><br />In a way a Remnant outbreak is a lazy choice for a main villain given that Landy traditionally brings in new villains in every book. However, once the outbreak gets going it actually becomes a gripping story in which Landy begins to show his ruthless side in relation to his characters. The plot moves quickly and contains exciting set pieces in the trademark Skulduggery Pleasant style. There are also a couple of juicy twists in terms of information about the overarching plotline, and as such it is difficult not to recommend the book as an excellent continuation of what is an excellent series. I chose to knock off a star considering the slow start, but by the end that really doesn't matter. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5836398620292052182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16289829005049235442" style="display:none">1) "What exactly would you call a dog" pg156<br /><br />2) This is the fifth and most current book in the already intriguing series, Derek Landy make this book thriling with the introduction as well as the much anticipated introduction of Lord Vile. As Valkyrie reveals this information to Skulduggery, she has tried to block her true name as well as blaock the possibility to be possessed but the visions by the sensitives has not yet changed. During this they encounter a man called Tesseract and they must stop him at all costs, or they will die. Tanith being possessed permanently was a very strong twist in the book.<br /><br />3) My favorite part of the novel is when Valkyrie and Skulduggery enquire Vaurien Scapgrace and they begin to tease him. Scapegrace has always hated them and wanted to kill them but they always elude him and make him very angry. Despite his efforts he can't seem to make them treat him seriously let alone the possibility that he could kill them. The connection i have made here is a book to book connection as i have seen this before in other novels.<br /><br />4) I would personally rate this book 5 stars because of its various humorous parts as well as the rising action and the constant increasing addictiveness </span>

  <span id="freeText9249450846583679507" style="display:none">After looking forward to redding this for a while and finally getting in the mood for it, I must say I was a bit disappointed. I found Mortal Coil to be the weakest book in the. Series so far. The plot was neither as fas paced or as fun as any of the previous ones. Also it was rather dark, which definitely wasn't something I appreciated. The humour helped as usual but I wish there was more of it to balance the gloom and doom. <br /><br />There was anew narrator for this book, which might also have contributed to my lesser enjoyment. Although this new guy (sorry, I don't remember the name) did a decent job and tried to be as close to Rupert Degas as possible he was still miles behind...<br /><br />This has still been an enjoyable read and I'm long forward to the next book in the series. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_659376801" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/659376801" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2329228-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433629372p2/2329228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/659376801?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/2329228-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer659376801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18105325544383382339">It's....it's.....<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427991i/855917._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379766060i/242532.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427991i/855918.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427991i/855919._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427991ra/855920.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/>A few of my previous complaints about this series have included - <br/><br/>1. Decrease in snappy humor<br/>2. Increase in tendency towards darkness <br/>3. General creepiness and kind of disturbing. <br/>4. Back of the cover was inappropriate<br/><br/><i>Mortal Coil</i> doesn't really stray from any of those problems. In fact, the front cover is a seriously creepy picture of Skulduggery's head and a whole bunch of skeleton and human hands reaching for it. I've been trying to keep it face down as much as possible, which</span>
  <span id="freeText18105325544383382339" style="display:none">It's....it's.....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427991i/855917._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379766060i/242532.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427991i/855918.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380427991i/855919._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380427991ra/855920.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>A few of my previous complaints about this series have included - <br><br>1. Decrease in snappy humor<br>2. Increase in tendency towards darkness <br>3. General creepiness and kind of disturbing. <br>4. Back of the cover was inappropriate<br><br><i>Mortal Coil</i> doesn't really stray from any of those problems. In fact, the front cover is a seriously creepy picture of Skulduggery's head and a whole bunch of skeleton and human hands reaching for it. I've been trying to keep it face down as much as possible, which is generally not a good sign. There is decidedly a lack of snappy humor in this book. It's not laugh-out-loud, crying-till-you-kicked-out-of-the-library sort of humor. There were maybe half a dozen comebacks that were genuinely funny. I think giggled more because I wanted something to giggle about then because it was that great. Heck, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17286896.Dark_Lord_A_Fiend_in_Need" title="Dark Lord A Fiend in Need by Jamie Thomson" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Lord: A Fiend in Need</a> made me laugh harder. No, this was definitely not like the first book in the series. <br>There is still Necromancer activity, possession by disturbing little Remnant things, and other dark things I did not fully appreciate.<br>Yet I gave it three stars. <br>I <i>liked</i> it? <br>Yeah, actually, I think I did. Despite the inappropriate cover, it was a tinge less darker, less morbid then the preceding book. It was less comical, true, but there is more character change. Stephanie/Valkyrie doesn't spend hours bemoaning about how she's "fooling her parents". There were less "deep dark hints" into Skulduggery's "evil past". In fact, I like how the "philosophical" nature in some ways adds to the story. Can the future be changed? What drives a person to become totally, whacked out evil? Can Valkyrie prevent herself from becoming Darquesse and destroying the world? Is it right to hurt a mortal, innocent person if they are being controlled by an evil being? What do you do when one of your best friends is controlled by a Remnant and dating a really awful guy? <br>That is, I think, why I enjoyed this book more. It's transformed itself from silly humor and emotionally irritating scenes of self-doubt to a more natural and questioning balance. Valkyrie is now a trained warrior. There is no more little girl learning about magic for the first time. She's building deep relationships with her friends. <br>Landy is also not afraid to murder off key characters. Well, mostly key. We haven't exactly seen Skulduggery's death yet (actually...he's already dead but that's not quite what I meant) but other main-ish characters die or get possessed and Valkyrie and Skulduggery are injured. As an author, he's not afraid to deal harm to his characters and I'm beginning to learn....that is an important aspect in truly tugging at your reader's emotions. <br><br>That said....WHYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYY IS THERE A RANDOM VAMPIRE-SORT-OF-KIND-OF-LOVE-TRIANGLE??????????<br>It wasn't really...needed. I have a feeling Caelan is being set up to be a more important foil in later books and that he might, in fact, do something to help turn her into Darquesse. However, I wanted to <i>gag</i>. REALLY, must Valkyrie turn into a pile of mush because a vampire kissed her? I'm not kidding. This is just disturbing on <i>so</i> many levels. It wasn't embedded in the plot enough to make me want to minus a star, but it was still there and it still made me go -<br>&gt;.&gt;<br>Stupid.<br>Very, very stupid. <br><br><br>I thought I was done with the series after the last book, but curiosity eventually won over and I got <i>Mortal Coil</i>. However, if the series continues to have such inappropriate covers I can't continue bringing them home. I'm going to have to seriously consider whether that means I stop reading the books until I have my own apartment where there aren't little siblings to take peeks at what their elder sister is reading or if the very fact that I feel the need to hide the covers from them means it is something *I* shouldn't be reading. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18105325544383382339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_590046737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/590046737" />
    <a title="Michael Cattigan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4539230-michael-cattigan"><img alt="Michael Cattigan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596819263p2/4539230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/590046737?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Cattigan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Cattigan" href="/user/show/4539230-michael-cattigan">Michael Cattigan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4539230-michael-cattigan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4539230-michael-cattigan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4539230-michael-cattigan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4539230-michael-cattigan?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer590046737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5653640809476871032">I have been enjoying this series. They were nothing exciting, nothing terribly original. <br/><br/>But they were fun. <br/><br/>They were light hearted. <br/><br/>They were fast-paced and witty. <br/><br/>But niggles and worries are starting to mar my enjoyment of them now. The worse elements are coming to the fore and the books are becoming increasingly dark, violent and disturbing. <br/><br/><br/><br/><a href='http://bookloverssanctuary.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/20130413-133658.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417588i/826150.jpg' alt='20130413-133658.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The plot focuses much more on Valkyrie Cain than the previous books: the threat doesn't come from an escaped convict or a malicious gaggle of vengefu</span>
  <span id="freeText5653640809476871032" style="display:none">I have been enjoying this series. They were nothing exciting, nothing terribly original. <br><br>But they were fun. <br><br>They were light hearted. <br><br>They were fast-paced and witty. <br><br>But niggles and worries are starting to mar my enjoyment of them now. The worse elements are coming to the fore and the books are becoming increasingly dark, violent and disturbing. <br><br><br><br><a href="http://bookloverssanctuary.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/20130413-133658.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417588i/826150.jpg" alt="20130413-133658.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The plot focuses much more on Valkyrie Cain than the previous books: the threat doesn't come from an escaped convict or a malicious gaggle of vengeful past characters; no one is attempting to return the Faceless Ones to power. Instead, the novel continues the quest to identify the new threat Darquesse and develops Valkyrie's final realisation from Dark Days that her true name is Darquesse and that she is herself destined to kill her own family and destroy the world. <br><br>Two parallel plots develop: Valkyrie seeks to have her true name sealed in order to stop anyone from forcing her to become Darquesse by using the power of her name; and the Necromancers accidentally release two thousand 'Remnants' into Ireland. Remnants, which had been introduced the <em>Dark Days</em> are slivers of dark power capable of inhabiting human bodies and accessing their skills, powers and memories.<br><br>It is the first strand of these plots that I balked at: in order to seal net true name, Valkyrie had to enter a state of conscious death, had to watch and observe her own dissection, the removal of her heart and the etching of symbol magic into the flesh of her heart. And the dead / undead surgeon Nye then proceeds to imprison Valkyrie and continue to dissect her organ by organ. And she lies there and watches the procedure in a state of inertia. <br><br>I'm sorry. <br><br>That's grim. <br><br>There's a lingering on it which hadn't been there in the darker aspects of the earlier novels . Yes, to be sure, Tanith Low is regularly tortured (I think as revenge on the editors who thought it was too dark to kill her off in book one); Skulduggery is tortured. But these are brief moments, usually off stage, referred to but not seen. <em>Here</em>, Landy lingers and describes and we see the heart. And, whilst dissected, Valkyrie contrives to escape her bonds, standing up, organs removed, folding her sternum and chest back onto itself, chucking her own heart and removed organs into a carrier bag. <br><br>This is almost torture-porn. <br><br>And for children. <br><br>I'm not the sort of chap who thinks children's books should be sentimentalised and anodyne. I like gritty young adult books: I thought <em>Between Shades of Gray</em>, fir example, was wonderful in its honest unsentimental realistic horror of the war. Violence, loss, death are, in my opinion not inappropriate for young adult fiction, if there is a point to it. <br><br>But this, like Darren Shan's <em>Demonata</em> series revelled in gore for its own sake and there <strong>was</strong> no other point. The gore did not make the situation tense; it did not add to the plot; it did not develop any character - although apparently Nye, the 'doctor' who performed the procedure will be brought back in future books. <br><br>In retrospect, perhaps it would be more accurate to say that I object to the pointlessness of Landy's torture-fest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5653640809476871032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tokio Myers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tokio Myers" href="/user/show/28412182-tokio-myers">Tokio Myers</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28412182-tokio-myers?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1531479397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9129529642183819894">In a remarkable change of events I am still in love with a skeleton. Which is odd for me since the majority of the time I like living breathing people but whatever. <br/><br/>This my friends, was a fantastic book. Something that's really hard to achieve seeing that it's the sixth book in a series. All the charm and dark dry humor is still here along with some new developments that keep you entertained. Be warned though, if you expect the nice sweet ending that we have learned to expect out of the Skuldugg</span>
  <span id="freeText9129529642183819894" style="display:none">In a remarkable change of events I am still in love with a skeleton. Which is odd for me since the majority of the time I like living breathing people but whatever. <br /><br />This my friends, was a fantastic book. Something that's really hard to achieve seeing that it's the sixth book in a series. All the charm and dark dry humor is still here along with some new developments that keep you entertained. Be warned though, if you expect the nice sweet ending that we have learned to expect out of the Skulduggery series then you are in for a disappointment. Mortal Coil is darker, bloodier, and heart breaking. <br /><br />If I were to complain about something it is the absence of Skulduggery. He still is around helping Valkyrie just not to the extant of the other books. This is (probably) because Valkyrie has grown as a person and doesn't need the detective to help her all the time. Good for her but I still want y skeleton to save some peoples asses with humor, luck, and lack of eyeballs. <br /><br />Quotes that mad me laugh out loud:<br /><br />“Stairs," Valkyrie said, disappointed.<br />"Not just ordinary stairs," Skulduggery told her as he led the way down. "Magic stairs."<br />"Really?"<br />"Oh, yes."<br />She followed him into the darkness. "How are they magic?"<br />"They just are."<br />"In what way?"<br />"In a magicky way."<br />She glared at the back of his head. "They aren't magic at all, are they?"<br />"Not really.”<br /><br /><br />“I need a weapon,” Valkyrie muttered.<br />“You’re an Elemental with a Necromancer ring, trained in<br />a variety of martial arts by some of the best ﬁghters in the world,” Skulduggery pointed out. “I’m fairly certain that makes you a weapon.”<br />“I mean a weapon you hold. You have a gun, Tanith has a sword... I want a stick.”<br />“I’ll buy you a stick for Christmas.” <br /><br /><br />“I find it rude to laugh at a man with a sword.” <br /><br /><br />“Personally, I think knees should be kept for the eighth or ninth date, or the wedding day. As a nice surprise you know? 'oh, my darling, you have knees! I never would have thought”<br /><br /><br />“She’s not… She’s not datin’ the skeleton, is she? How would that be even possible, let alone… nice? He’s got no skin, or lips, or… or nothin’.”<br /><br /><br />My personal favorite:<br /><br />“But he's in shackles, right? You beat him?"<br />"I like to think I beat him in a moral sense, in that he's an assassin and I'm not, but apart from that, no, not really.”<br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277591943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3835021212279873609">W-O-W. Derek Landy has outdone himself with <i>Mortal Coil</i>, the fifth and my personal favourite so far of the <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> series. Skulduggery and the gang are forced to deal with an invasion of body-snatching remnants while Valkyrie goes on a mission to seal her true name before it can be used against her... and the entire world.<br/><br/>Things get darker in this novel and there's some truly horrifying scenes that had me reading through the night to find out what happened next just so I could sleep</span>
  <span id="freeText3835021212279873609" style="display:none">W-O-W. Derek Landy has outdone himself with <i>Mortal Coil</i>, the fifth and my personal favourite so far of the <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> series. Skulduggery and the gang are forced to deal with an invasion of body-snatching remnants while Valkyrie goes on a mission to seal her true name before it can be used against her... and the entire world.<br /><br />Things get darker in this novel and there's some truly horrifying scenes that had me reading through the night to find out what happened next just so I could sleep easy. But as always, there's also some fantastically funny scenes that kept me reading just because I wanted to. There's also a lot more romance creeping into the story - and I'm a sucker for romance when it's done well. Gotta say, as far as Valkyrie is concerned, I'm a Fletcher girl. Caelan is a little too shifty and suspicious for my liking! But Tanith and Ghastly? Adorable. Landy must've ripped out my heart a dozen times by the end of the book regarding those two, but I'm still holding out hope.<br /><br />Can't wait to see where Landy takes the series next. Even though I have my own theories (on Darquesse; on Valkyrie's reflection; on the Fletcher/Val/Caelan triangle) I'm sure he'll still manage to surprise me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3835021212279873609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175936837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7645063263977288913">Skulduggery is back! He is just a very good and interesting character! Actually the story isn't that important somehow, i mean it's good and well thought through. But the interesting part is the interaction between those great characters! Most of the time it's not laughing out loud funny, it's kind of a quiet sarcasm and irony. Which suits the story and the characters very well. And you cannot know for sure whether they are good or evil. You just hope that they are good but even Skulduggery has </span>
  <span id="freeText7645063263977288913" style="display:none">Skulduggery is back! He is just a very good and interesting character! Actually the story isn't that important somehow, i mean it's good and well thought through. But the interesting part is the interaction between those great characters! Most of the time it's not laughing out loud funny, it's kind of a quiet sarcasm and irony. Which suits the story and the characters very well. And you cannot know for sure whether they are good or evil. You just hope that they are good but even Skulduggery has a very dark side in him and Valkyrie as well. I enjoy that immensely! That actually gives it quite a realistic feeling, although they are all characters from a magical world. <br />What i did not so much liked this time was the fighting. Over half the book are descriptions of fights. Interesting and sometimes funny ones, but near the end it felt a bit boring and overused. I wish Landy have had other ideas of having a face to face conflict between characters, maybe just a different kind of physical fight,to give it another feeling. <br />Still, i think this series is highly entertaining and Skulduggery is one of the best mail character ever! </span>
  <a data-text-id="7645063263977288913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText757732081369098220" style="display:none">All hell breaks loose in this novel. If you haven't started reading this series yet, then I insist that you do! This one has amped up the evil and the creepiness with the remnants (which are featured in another book) taking over bodies. <br /><br />One thing that has changed which wasn't really in the others is the amount of kissing in this. I don't mind a good kissing session in a book but I think that maybe younger teenage boys who have been reading the series may be put off by it. I am also seeing some 'Twilight' in this with the whole 'Vampire being gorgeous and in love with the main character', I was a bit disappointed as I recall the Vampires being scary in the first book not cute. <br /><br />There was a sad-ish moment towards the end which I won't give away but I am a little upset about it. And there's a small cliffhanger at the end, so I'm really looking forward to the next one. Landy has out done himself with this one, Bring on the Death Bringer! </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007326013" href="/book/show/9767135-mortal-coil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21724974-emily?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer677798621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16145988779186337979">That one was well good. I feel like the series takes a turn for the very dark at #5, probably because of the Remnants. It's really interesting, all the themes of darkness within, who we are, how darkness can latch on inside us. Is it a part of you (like Darquesse) or an external force (like a Remnant?).<br/><br/>I forgot how much I love Fletcher. Annoying, yes, but adorable!<br/><br/>Also, these books are still ridiculously funny. Reading them in public = laughing all over the place! <br/><br/>Rereading them as an adult I'm </span>
  <span id="freeText16145988779186337979" style="display:none">That one was well good. I feel like the series takes a turn for the very dark at #5, probably because of the Remnants. It's really interesting, all the themes of darkness within, who we are, how darkness can latch on inside us. Is it a part of you (like Darquesse) or an external force (like a Remnant?).<br /><br />I forgot how much I love Fletcher. Annoying, yes, but adorable!<br /><br />Also, these books are still ridiculously funny. Reading them in public = laughing all over the place! <br /><br />Rereading them as an adult I'm noticing lots of interesting things, for example the multiple third person POV. It's fab -- we go all over, in the heads of all the MCs and also the heads of random people who never reappear, which sounds like a dodgy technique, but works really well, because Landy writes everything with such wit and humour. The one person whose POV we never experience is Skulduggery, despite his being the eponymous character. I don't know what to surmise from this, but it's fascinating!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16145988779186337979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2808797420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13517626561457946396">Skulduggery Pleasant Book 5<br/>*Mortal Coil* by Derek Landy<br/>This goes without saying, Mortal Coil has a crazy subservant plot for the series and it is full on action with a lot of primary 'Skulduggery Pleasant' elements and Derek Landy boldly establishes the fact about where the series is currently heading and it's evident it's halfway through and things are already getting much darker than I could have suspected. I mean, the story is wild and unleashed, the book introduces some formidable and memora</span>
  <span id="freeText13517626561457946396" style="display:none">Skulduggery Pleasant Book 5<br />*Mortal Coil* by Derek Landy<br />This goes without saying, Mortal Coil has a crazy subservant plot for the series and it is full on action with a lot of primary 'Skulduggery Pleasant' elements and Derek Landy boldly establishes the fact about where the series is currently heading and it's evident it's halfway through and things are already getting much darker than I could have suspected. I mean, the story is wild and unleashed, the book introduces some formidable and memorable secondary characters which give the book a thrill. Major character developments include Valkyrie, Skul, Ghastly(immense), Tanith, China, Solomon and the Sanctuary. I mean, it's really shocking, at least for me to see how much things have changed since the start of the book. By the time you reach the end you will be blown away by the shock and the surprise of it all, things are getting far worse. About the narration and writing, it is top-notch, better than all the previous book but to be honest it does not feel like a typical Skulduggery Pleasant novel, perhaps because the general lack of optimism and lustrous humor does not frequent the pages. Derek throws in some impressive quotes, lines, dialogues with the usual twists in the story as well as makes the secondary characters feel very important, I was very much involved and engrossed in the book, mostly for it's fast-paced action, unfaltering narration and of course, first class character evolution. 'Mortal Coil' takes the threat upto a more higher level with really powerful enemies the 'Remnants' possessing friends and foes alike of our friends. The book really does get pretty dark and gritty with all the violence and breakout in Ireland and major character deaths like Kenspeckle Grouse, Sanctuary Leader. It is indeed shocking to see that almost half of the Sanctuary including the elders and leader have been changed twice through the book owing to the deaths of the predecessors. This was a wild ride for me, for real. I will never be able to perceive Skulduggery, Tanith and Valkyrie as I did in the previous books. All of these characters have become older and more serious than before and that really creeps me out. Shoutout to Tesseract, a primary antagonist in the book. I really respect his character, no personal vendettas and purely professional drives. He really went of out respectably in the final chapter.Tesseract will be one of the most memorable characters from the series but I wished he stayed for a book or two more. As the series is mostly plot and character driven it has really been difficult for me to review the writing style and which elements I like and don't like because I read not from the point of view of a reviewer/critic but a reader looking to devour the series ASAP thanks to the total insanity of the plot. It is notable that the book is a bit bigger than the earlier books. Also, the whole 'Death Bringer', 'Lord Vile' and 'Darkquesse' plot points are very much highlighted, especially after the first half and I really hate this, Mr. Landy reminds the readers of the dark fate(the apocalypse led by Val/Darkq) and how it is inevitable. I'm really sad for Tanith(cuz she's a Remnant now) and I get why Mr. Landy kept Sanguine and other minor vile's alive because of the role they'll play in shaping Darkquesse. The book introduced a lot about the past like the League of Dead Men, the binding of the Remnants, Gordon Edgly's life and habits and the world before the Great War which adds depth to the story and makes it way more interesting and surreal. I really like the Remnant plot and how it progressed, i was always o the edge of my seat to see who the Remnants would posses next and how it would all play out by the end and was anxious if my favorite characters would survive until the end. We even got a glimpse of Darkquesse and Lord Vile (jumping to next book as soon as I type this out). Seeing the Remnants posses a multitude of characters was really cool and the author described the whole event very well right from the beginning, the one mistake Wreath made and turned the whole Shebang into hazardous crises for Ireland. I'm really anxious about the remainder of the series and look forward to enjoy the Skeleton detective and Valkyrie kick some serious ass without upsetting the power balance once again. i simply can't getting better than it is. Nice Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13517626561457946396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167669788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167669788" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167669788?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=whodunit-supernatural">whodunit-supernatural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167669788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16797915065661282320">3 1/2<br/><br/>This is one of those times where I wish we could do a review for the whole series.<br/><br/>This is a fun, action-packed middle-grade series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton/wizard detective, and his young apprentice/partner, Valkyrie Cain. There's a lot going on, and every book, generally, gets a little bit better and, to a surprising degree, a little bit darker. <br/><br/>There's a lot of death and mayhem, and the stakes are raised with every book. But while the general goings on are fairly predicta</span>
  <span id="freeText16797915065661282320" style="display:none">3 1/2<br /><br />This is one of those times where I wish we could do a review for the whole series.<br /><br />This is a fun, action-packed middle-grade series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton/wizard detective, and his young apprentice/partner, Valkyrie Cain. There's a lot going on, and every book, generally, gets a little bit better and, to a surprising degree, a little bit darker. <br /><br />There's a lot of death and mayhem, and the stakes are raised with every book. But while the general goings on are fairly predictable, there are enough twitsts and turns that will keep you guessing and on your toes. <br /><br />My one major complaint is that I don't really connect emotionally with the characters. I like the characters - they're funny and snarky - but there's a lot more focus on the goings on and less on the characters thoughts or feelings.<br /><br />This does seem to be changing a bit, and as Valkyrie gets older there seems to be more attention being paid to the consequences of her actions, not just physically (which are a little too easily remedied in the books thus far), but emotionally. I do hope that the trend continues and we start things getting a bit deeper as the series progresses.<br /><br />That said, I can't believe what happened at the end of the 5th book, and after reading the first five in short order, I can't wait I have to wait, now, to find out what happens! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16797915065661282320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VR3Z/kx3LI8t3xFyGl6mSkfOdZ6kF4VGnH/eITMuXTtfDD0fA/J7HGhdJBN7oDw9BsUP1Q0WIO15F83perj+kQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0xA/R+zEGNXBWY+J+609ankjx/NPoiNcRdWPcbTSxAXZAdumo0FPRoTbuuiaU6cdOCi9uOajhvegvZy5/URnrw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer637114765555358441">Derek Landy is an Irish writer and screenwriter. In addition to the bestselling children's/YA series of <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> books, a supernatural mystery series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton detective, and Valkyrie Cain, a young female magician, he has written two screenplays that have been made into films: the IFTA award winning "Dead Bodies" and the IFTA nominated "Boy Eats Girl". L</span>
  <span id="freeText637114765555358441" style="display:none">Derek Landy is an Irish writer and screenwriter. In addition to the bestselling children's/YA series of <i>Skulduggery Pleasant</i> books, a supernatural mystery series starring Skulduggery Pleasant, a skeleton detective, and Valkyrie Cain, a young female magician, he has written two screenplays that have been made into films: the IFTA award winning "Dead Bodies" and the IFTA nominated "Boy Eats Girl". Landy himself was nominated for an IFTA for Best Script. <br /><br />He doesn’t like to brag about all the awards he’s won, such as the Irish Book of the Decade, or the Red House in the UK, or all the other awards that he humbly displays on his mantelpiece. He is also far too modest to mention things like the first book being a Publisher’s Weekly Best Book of the Year, but would like to extend an invitation to Oprah to pop around one day for tea, in thanks for selecting his book for the Oprah’s Book Club Kids Reading List. <br /><br />Derek plays too many video games, reads too many comics, and watches too many movies. He lives in Ireland with too many cats. Occasionally he talks to real people, but only when he absolutely has to.</span>
